As shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202403642-fig-0006">6f</a>, the full cell exhibited a maximal energy density of 231.2&nbsp;W&nbsp;h&nbsp;kg<sup>−1</sup> at a power density of 24.41&nbsp;W&nbsp;kg<sup>−1</sup>. Even at a maximal power density of 741.1&nbsp;W&nbsp;kg<sup>−1</sup>, the full cell still maintains a high energy density of 142.7&nbsp;W&nbsp;h&nbsp;kg<sup>−1</sup>, indicating the promising application prospects of NVP//PCHC-10 in the future.</div>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="adfm202403642-fig-0006"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/d11fe7da-fd53-4583-b2cd-c8f269d0fa3b/adfm202403642-fig-0006-m.jpg"><picture>

      </section>
      <section class="article-section__content" id="adfm202403642-sec-0030">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="adfm202403642-sec-0030-title">3 Conclusion</h2>
         
         <p>In summary, PCHC-10 with abundant of appropriately closed pore size (0.45&nbsp;nm) and nano-scaled soft carbon coating layer was precisely engineered through a chemical crosslink reaction involving pre-oxidized phenolic resin and a small quantity of pitch. The detailed correlation analysis has been made and demonstrated that the closed volume and the closed pore size are the key indicators of effecting the electrochemical performance in SIBs. As anode material, PCHC-10 exhibited a high specific capacity of 359.8&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, and a high plateau capacity of 242.8&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> below 0.15&nbsp;V, significantly surpassing that of HC anode. In addition, the PCHC-10 anode exhibited excellent cycling performance for 100 cycles (91.4% capacity retention). Furthermore, DFT models with various closed pore sizes ranging from 0.0 to 0.9&nbsp;nm have been rationally constructed, revealing that the HC material with a closed pore size of 0.45&nbsp;nm exhibited the best Na<sup>+</sup> adsorption ability. Moreover, the as-assembled NVP//PCHC-10 full cell delivered a high specific capacity (109.1 and 67.5&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> at 0.1 and 3&nbsp;C, respectively), superior rate performance (61.9% capacity retention) as well as good cycling stability. The full cell exhibited a maximal energy density of 231.2&nbsp;Wh&nbsp;kg<sup>−1</sup> at 24.41&nbsp;W&nbsp;kg<sup>−1</sup>, and a maximal power density of 741.1&nbsp;W&nbsp;kg<sup>−1</sup> at 142.7&nbsp;W&nbsp;h&nbsp;kg<sup>−1</sup>. We are convinced that this work will offer a new thinking in designing novel HC materials and enhancing the energy densities and power density of SIBs to a new level.</p>
         </section>
      <section class="article-section__content" id="adfm202403642-sec-0040">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="adfm202403642-sec-0040-title">4 Experimental Section</h2>
         
         <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="adfm202403642-sec-0050">
            
            <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="adfm202403642-sec-0060">
               
               <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="adfm202403642-sec-0070">
                  
                  <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section4" id="adfm202403642-sec-0070-title"> Fabrication of Pre-Oxidized Phenolic Resin</h4>
                  
                  <p>Typically, phenolic resin purchased from Henan Borun New Material Co. was placed in a muffle furnace and calcined in air at 250&nbsp;°C for 12&nbsp;h to pre-oxidized. Subsequently, pre-oxidized phenolic resin was obtained by mixing the pre-oxidized material and zirconia beads in a ball-milling jar at a mass ratio of 1:100 and grinding in a ball mill at 800&nbsp;rpm for 2&nbsp;h.</p>
                  </section>
               
               <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="adfm202403642-sec-0080">
                  
                  <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section4" id="adfm202403642-sec-0080-title"> Fabrication of PCHC-x</h4>
                  
                  <p>Soft carbon-coated HC materials were obtained by calcining the mixture of pre-oxidized phenolic resin with pitch (SAXD-280X, purchased from Shenzhen Kejingzhida Technology Co.) at 1200 °C for 1&nbsp;h under Ar gas atmosphere. The resulting samples were denoted as PCHC-x (x is the weight ratio of pitch), where the weight ratio of pitch added was 5%, 10%, and 20%, respectively. For comparison, HC material was also prepared by direct carbonization of pre-oxidized phenolic resin under the same conditions as PCHC-x.</p>
                  </section>
               
               <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="adfm202403642-sec-0090">
                  
                  <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section4" id="adfm202403642-sec-0090-title"> Materials Characterizations</h4>
                  
                  <p>The detailed surface morphologies of these as-prepared PCHC-x and HC materials were observed by SEM (ZEISS GeminiSEM 300). The corresponding microstructural information and micropore structures were also tested by HRTEM (FEI F20). The detailed microcrystalline structures were characterized by XRD (Bruker D8 Advance) with Cu Ka radiation (λ = 1.5406&nbsp;Å) and Raman spectra (Horiba XploRA) with a 514.5&nbsp;nm laser excitation. The total SSA and the corresponding pore-size distribution were examined on N<sub>2</sub> sorption surface area tester (JW-BK222, Beijing JWGB) and calculated through the Brunauer−Emmett−Teller (BET) method. XPS analysis was also used to measure the elemental composition of the as-obtained samples on Thermo Fisher K-Alpha American with an Al Kα X-ray source. Pyrolysis behaviors for these samples were obtained by TGA on NETZSCH, STA409PC from 30 to 900&nbsp;°C under Ar. FTIR was performed in Bruker VERTEX 80&nbsp;V at scanning frequency 32 and resolution 2&nbsp;cm<sup>−1</sup>.</p>
                  </section>
               
               <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="adfm202403642-sec-0100">
                  
                  <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section4" id="adfm202403642-sec-0100-title"> Electrochemical Measurements of Half-Cells</h4>
                  
                  <p>CR2032 coin cells were fabricated to evaluate the electrochemical performance of HC anode. The anode slurry was prepared by mixing 90 wt% HC materials, 5 wt% carbon black (CB), and 5 wt% sodium-alginate in an aqueous solution. The homogenous slurry was then casted on Cu foil, and the mass loading of active materials was kept at 1 and 4.5&nbsp;mg&nbsp;cm<sup>−2</sup>, respectively. Then, the electrodes were dried in a vacuum oven at 90&nbsp;°C for 12&nbsp;h. During the assembly of half cells, sodium metal foil was used as the counter electrode, 1&nbsp;<span class="smallCaps">m</span>&nbsp;NaClO<sub>4</sub> in ethylene (EC) and diethyl carbonate (DEC) (1:1 in volume) with 5% fluoroethylene carbonate (FEC) as the electrolyte, and glass fiber (GF/D) purchased from Whatman as the separator, and all the assembly processes were performed in a glove box (H<sub>2</sub>O, O<sub>2</sub> &lt; 0.1&nbsp;ppm). The GCD measurement and GITT were detected by the BTS3000 battery test system with 0.001–2.5&nbsp;V. CV curves at various scan rates from 0.1 to 1.0&nbsp;mV&nbsp;s<sup>–1</sup> and EIS measurements in the frequency range from 0.01 HZ to 100 KHz were conducted on a CHI660D electrochemical workstation.</p>
                  </section>
               
               <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="adfm202403642-sec-0110">
                  
                  <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section4" id="adfm202403642-sec-0110-title"> Electrochemical Measurements of Full Cells</h4>
                  
                  <p>The full cell of Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>//PCHC-10 was assembled using a pre-sodium treated PCHC-10 anode and Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> cathode in a glove box. The pre-sodium treated PCHC-10 anode was obtained by direct contact with metal Na foil in 100&nbsp;µL electrolyte for 1&nbsp;h. The Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> cathode slurry was prepared by homogeneous mixing the 80 wt% Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>, 10 wt% CB and 10 wt% polyvinylidene fluoride (PVDF) in N-Methyl pyrrolidone (NMP) solution, and then the slurry was coated on Al foil and dried in a vacuum oven at 90&nbsp;°C for 12&nbsp;h to obtain the Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> cathode. In addition, the mass ratio of anode to cathode in full cells was controlled at 1:1.15, and the test voltage of the full cell was 2.0–4.0&nbsp;V in the BTS3000 battery test system.</p>
                  </section>
               
               <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="adfm202403642-sec-0120">
                  
                  <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section4" id="adfm202403642-sec-0120-title"> DFT Calculations</h4>
                  
                  <p>The DFT calculation in this work was performed using the CASTEP module in Materials Studio. A double-layer graphite crystal cell structure with 128 carbon atoms per layer was established, with all atoms relaxed. A 15&nbsp;Å vacuum layer was established vertically to avoid the influence between periodic structures in the z-direction. The generalized gradient approximation (GGA) – Perdew–Burke–Ernzerhof (PBE) formulation was used in the adsorption process of sodium on the double-layer carbon structure to describe the exchange-correlation energies. The convergence criteria for geometry optimization of all models were as follows: the self-consistent field energy of 2×10<sup>−5</sup> Hartree, energy gradient of 0.005&nbsp;Hartree&nbsp;Å<sup>−1,</sup> and maximum atomic displacement of 0.002&nbsp;Å. After testing different k-point grid schedules, a Monkhorst-Pack grid of 2×2×1 was used to sample the surface Brillouin zone.</p>
                  </section>
               
               <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="adfm202403642-sec-0130">
                  
                  <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section4" id="adfm202403642-sec-0130-title"> Statistical Analysis</h4>
                  
                  <p>The FTIR, XRD, SAXS, true density, N<sub>2</sub> adsorption-desorption, open pore size distribution, and XPS data are original data. The close pore sizes distribution, and Raman data are obtained by normalized from original data.</p>
                  </section>
               </section>
            </section>
         </section>
